text:
I originally submitted this recipe.  I've been experimenting and have found a healthier low fat version that's just as delicious: 1/4 butter (instead of 1 cup) and 1 can of evaporated skim milk (instead of cream). Turns out lighter but just as delicious. I've also used white fish, scallops and prawns in place of the chicken sometimes!

text:
This recipes was delicious!  I made a few changes, mostly to keep the number of pans down.  I carmelized the onions in a large pan, then I added the rest of the butter, tomato sauce, cream, and spices and simmered (on EXTREMELY low heat) for about 10 minutes. Then I added the ckicken bits right into the sauce mixture (without tandoori masala) and let it simmer on low for about 25 more minutes until the chicken was done, being careful not to boil the cream.  The chicken was tender and the sauce was delicious. I served it over basmati rice and garnished with fresh cilantro. My husband loved it! One of the best Indian recipes I've found.

text:
This was SO good!! And easy! I cut down on the dishes and made this all in my cast iron dutch oven. I caramelized the onions and garlic in the butter, once they were done I removed them to a bowl and deglazed the pan with a little chicken broth. Made the sauce as directed and once it was hot, I added the chicken. I didn't have any tandoori masala so I marinated the chicken pieces in a mixture of yogurt, lemon juice, garam masala, cayenne and curry powder for a couple of hours. Turned out great!!

text:
Loved it! It was delicious!! I changed it up a bit after reading other reviews: 1/4 cup butter (instead of 1 cup) 1 can fat free evaporated milk (instead of 3 cups heavy cream) 1/2 teaspoon salt (instead of 2 teaspoons) 1/2 teaspoon cayenne pepper (instead of 1 teaspoon) and 1 tablespoon curry powder (instead of garam masala, which I could not find)  I omitted the vegetable oil and tandoori masala.  I cooked it all in one pot like someone else had suggested. Caramelized the onions with 2 tablespoons butter and set them aside, deglazed the pan with a little bit of chicken broth (low sodium kind), added the rest of the butter, tomato sauce, evaporated milk, salt, cayenne and curry. Stirred it, added cut up raw chicken, and then simmered for 25 min. Then stirred in the onions. It was fantastic over basmati rice, I would definitely make it again!!

We reaaaaally loved this one.  I couldn't believe that these smells were coming out of my kitchen!  I never thought I would be able to do this, but it was super simple and really delicious.  I also stirred in a 5 oz can of evaporated skim milk (after turning off the heat in the end) instead of using the heavy cream.  I tried stirring it in in the middle, but if you don't have something with enough fat (like cream), then everything curdles.  Trust me, I learned my lesson, twice.  This tastes like a tikka masala.  Served with basmati and store-bought naan.

text:
I love Indian food, and it's tough to recreate the yummy restaurant flavors at home -- believe me when I say I've tried, and I know how to cook.  This recipe is so good and so easy that I'm stunned.  Changes I made: Used rotisserie chicken and mixed the pieces of chicken with the tandoori masala, let it sit in the fridge while preparing the rest of the recipe, then threw in the chicken at the end; cut the salt in half; used twice as much tomato sauce, not as much cream (two thirds, maybe?), doubled the spices, used half the onion, and added a package of frozen chopped spinach.  I  think the secret to this recipe that makes such a HUGE difference is the tandoori masala (this is the one ingredient that I've never used in previous attempts, and always mixed my own spices -- no more!), but whatever it is, I'm madly grateful for this recipe.  In all sincerity, this recipe makes chicken makhani (I've made it "saag" style with the spinach) equally as well as most that I've had.  Wow, and well done, mn!!  Thank you so much for sharing this gem of a recipe!

text:
This is a pretty good recipe for butter chicken as listed. I am appalled that some reviewers have noted making a substitution of curry powder for the Garam Masala and or the Tandori Masala. These are both an unacceptable substitutes and will not yield good results. Curry powder was invented by British spice companies as a way to mimic Indian flavors and is not an actual Indian ingredient substituting it is all wrong for this recipe. If you are having problems locating the essential Indian ingredients try to find a local Indian market; Almost every town big enough to have an Indian restaurant will have at least one.

So good!!!!!  This smells and tastes delicious. I make the lightened version with evaporated milk and less butter.  Since I can't find tandoori masala I substitute curry.  I serve this over rice with garlic naan. Tastes like it came from a restaurant but this is soooo easy.  Thanks for sharing this great recipe! I wanted to add that I make this all the time now (1xweek usually) and I have streamlined prep to save time and cut down on the number of pots/pans.  After I carmelize the onions/garlic, I add the chicken chunks which I've tossed in oil and curry (subbed for the tandoori masala).  Once the chicken is cooked, I add the liquid ingredients to the pot and simmer them.

text:
This recipe is one of our absolute favourites, the kids even ask for seconds!!  I did find that cooking the chicken in the oven took way longer than 12 minutes, it was more like 35.  So now I sear it in a frying pan with the Tandoori and then add it to the sauce to simmer for 30 mins (which also cuts down on the amount of dishes).  I've made it with all the fatty products, as well as 1/2 the butter and 10% cream and it's just as good both ways.  I'm going to try the evaporated skim milk to see how that goes next time.  The sauce freezes great, so I always double up on the chicken breasts so there is enough for next time.

text:
This recipe is FABULOUS - even better than my local Indian restaurant! It has just enough kick to be appropriate for the whole family. I grilled the chicken and cut it into bite-sized pieces the night before. The next day, I caramelized the onions and garlic, shook the cooked chicken with tandoori masala in a plastic bag to coat it, then threw everything in a slow-cooker on low and didn't touch it for four hours. At dinner time, I gave it a thorough stirring and served over basmati rice - yum! This will now make regular appearances on my family's menu.

This is sooo good I just ate dinner and had to write a review! I used 3lbs chicken thighs, (big family) doubled the spices. No cayenne pepper so i put 1tsp of chili powder. Used a 28oz can of crushed tomatoes, 2 cups of whipping cream 1 cup of 2% milk. Sautee onions and garlic, then added a few tbsp of tomato paste. Didn't use butter at all because didn't have any (olive oil instead). Add spices to carmelized onion and sautee a few min., add raw chicken and cook everything together 5-10 min. Add crushed tomato, cream/milk and simmer on low an hour. WAS SOO GOOD with basmati rice. Try it.

I can't even express how much I love this recipe, 5 stars doesn't seem enough!  The first time I followed the recipe exactly, every other time I have used the healthier revisions suggested by the original poster mn and I like it even more and don't feel so guilty eating it now :) It truly does taste like authentic butter chicken, and I didn't need to purchase 30 different ingredients like some of the other recipes I found. My husband and I first had Butter Chicken in India on the road to see the Taj Majal in a small street side cafe.  We absolutely loved it and had it several more time over our 3 months we traveled in India.  Back in the states - we were unable to find really good butter chicken at the local Indian restaurants.  So I decided to take it upon myself to make it and this recipe was PERFECT!  I did follow the alternate directions that the original poster added (using 1/4 cup butter and evaporated milk instead of cream) - and the results were fantastic . My local store did not have the tandoori masala - so I just omitted it and added a little extra of the garam masala - but it probably would have enhanced the flavors even more.   I'll be on the lookout for the tandoori masala so I can make this again . It's definitely going in the 'rotation'.   I served it with Naan and even the kid loved it - especially when we told him he didn't have to use any silverware!  Definitely brought back good memories of our time in India!

text:
Amazing recipe.  Each and every time I make it, friends and family ooh and awe.  However, I've learned to skim down the calories and fat while adding to the taste, so here are some substitutions/amendments: 

Skip the butter and use olive oil to caramelize the onion and garlic.  For taste, use one to two tablespoons of butter for the sauce with the tomatoes, but substitute low-fat yogurt or skim milk for the heavy cream to reduce calories.  Lastly, I typically double or triple the spices because the fam likes things hot and savory.

text:
Made this using only 1/4 Cup butter and two tins of evaporated milk (=3 Cups).  I thought had made a mistake because it was SO saucy when I finished.  On top of that my milk curdled (saved afterwards by my immersion blender) because everything must've been too hot when the evaporated milk was added.  This made enough sauce for 2 1/2 lbs of chicken!!  I simmered and simmered until it was reasonably thick.  I'll make this again (but not too often as I'm sure it's still quite cholesterol laden).  I also added 1 tsp of ginger to my garlic/onion mixture.  It turns out my curdled milk/sauce was a happy accident.  I blended the sauce and everything, even the onions, etc. was pureed.  The sauce was rich and oh, so silky smooth!!  p.s. Only use an immersion blender if you want the sauce to be extra smooth, NOT a regular blender.  If you blend HOT sauce in a regular blender it will ERUPT in a scalding geyser, covering you and your kitchen!!

text:
Very good. I made this using the evaporated milk and 1/4 cup butter. After I added the milk and simmered for a while, it looked like the milk had curdled--I'm not sure if others have experienced this? But, I continued with the recipe anyway, and it turned out pretty well. If you are making the light version of this recipe, as others have noted, the cayenne pepper and the salt should be decreased--I'd say 1 or 1.5 tsp salt and maybe 3/4 tsp cayenne pepper. I couldn't find tandoori masala in my supermarket, so I made a spice rub of 1 tbs lemon juice, 2 tsp cumin, 2 tsp paprika, 2 tsp garlic powder, shake of coriander, 1 tsp chili powder. The spice rub was pretty good, but I think it was too flavorful and overpowered the delicious sauce. So next time I'll either try to find tandoori masala or maybe take another reviewer's suggestion and season with curry powder.

text:
It was so easy to make and outstanding.  I made some changes to conserve ingredients and it turned out so good, I have no idea if the original recipe would have been better, but I can't imagine it tasting any better than it did.

-I halved the sauce recipe.  I used 4 quite large chicken breasts and still had well more than enough sauce so I think with half the sauce recipe you could use as many as 6 reasonably sized chicken breasts.
-I used only 1/4 cup of butter in the sauce. I also only used one cup of heavy cream and half a cup of evaporated milk (I can't handle that much heavy cream!)
-I couldn't find tandoori masala at the store so I googled it to find its ingredients and made an approximate version of my own consisting of 1/8 tsp each of garam masala and ginger powder, a pinch of curry powder, and 1/4 tsp each of cayenne pepper powder and garlic powder and the zest of 1 lemon.  Again, I don't really know how real tandoori masala would have tasted but mine tasted so good I doubt I would spend the money to ever find out.

text:
This was my first attempt at cooking Indian food.  I read the original poster's lowfat version she posted and decided to try that. I used two pounds of chicken and three cups of evaporated milk. I cut the cayenne pepper in half, used only one half teaspoon salt and cut the butter to one fourth cup as was suggested for the low fat version. I followed the preparation instructions as suggested. Since I am a vegetarian, I did not try it, but my family all thought it was very good and close to what they like at the local Indian restaurants. It was a bit spicy for their palettes, so next time I will cut the spices. My daughter also thought I should add some tomato paste to the recipe. I served it with basmati rice with some peas mixed in and with some store bough naan. From my family's feedback, it was a good recipe.

I love the flavor of this recipe.  Don't rush the onions.  Truly carmelize them. It makes a difference.  The tandoori masala on the oven baked chicken is also what contributes to the full flavor profile.  I would not skip that step.  Now, I cannot find tandoori masala in my small town so I used the Tandoori Masala Spice Mix here on Allrecipes.  It worked very well.  I was only missing the fenugreek which I omitted.  I have prepared this twice. I will add about one-half pound more chicken which will need a little more tandoori.  A keeper.

I gave 4 stars only because of the modifications.
In an effort to healthify this recipe even more, I used Becel margarine instead of butter and used a moderate amount (1/4-1/3 cup).
I used a can of coconut milk instead of cream/evaporated milk.
I cooked the chicken partially with the onions and garlic after caramelizing, then added the sauce that I had simmering in another pot.

Sauce was a little on the thin side, but will simmer longer to hopefully reduce.
Smelled great, tasted quite nice.
Will definitely make again and again!

text:
I make this but use only apx. 4 pats of butter and use one small container of plain yogurt and 1/4 cup of heavy cream and also with the gram marsala add 1 teaspoon Indian curry.  I mix all the ingredients but the cream in a bowl and coat the chicken (I like my chicken on the bone)and place in a baking dish or a clay pot and pour sauce over chicken and bake I serve it with honey drizzled over top to take away the bitterness and bake at 325 unttil chicken is done and tender. I also used chopped tomatoes along with tomato sauce.

text:
My husband and I have made this many times, and now I see that the original creator has posted in the comments about how it has been lightened up with about 1/2 the butter and switching out the cream for evaporated skim milk.  I always just used half & half but if the evaporated milk doesn't change the flavor a lot, then I'm changing it next time I make it.  This dish is soooo good, and the leftovers the next day are even better!  I had 2 people at work ask me for the recipe and that was just based on how it SMELLED!  I serve it with basmati rice that contains a little butter, 7-8 cardamom seeds and some dried parsley.  Perfect Indian dinner!

text:
Everyone I cook for knows this as my specialty now, and it's my favorite thing that I make. First time I made it (I was new to cooking,) I misread the "1 teaspoon cayenne and 1 teaspoon garam masala" as one tablespoon of each...and it was the best mistake I ever made. Mind you, I do like it spicy, but if you do to I promise it's incredible that way. I use more garlic, as always, half the butter (that's plenty) and coconut milk instead of the heavy cream- better flavor that way. Give this recipe a try, you won't be sorry.

Yummy!  This was fantastic!  I did some small substitutions, instead of vegetable oil on the chicken I used plain yogurt.  I also pierced the chicken with a fork to tenderize it and let it marinate in the mixture for 4 hours before grilling on a hot grill.  As suggested by the originator of the recipe to make it lower calorie I used a can of evaporated milk and 1/4 cup of butter.  I also cut back on the cayenne to 1/2 tsp and found it pleasently spicy.  Thanks for such a great recipe!!

text:
This was fantastic! I, too, cut down on the number of dishes involved and on the fat. I added the chicken to the skillet after cooking the onions, then added the tomato sauce (actually, I found I had only one 8-oz can of tomato sauce, so I used that and a can of tomato paste), and the rest of the ingredients for the sauce. I added a little bit of brown sugar as some others suggested, and I let it simmer until the meat was cooked. Then I added some cauliflower and let it simmer again until that was cooked. To cut down on fat, I used only about 3.5 Tbsps. of butter initially to saute the onions, and I didn't add any more butter or oil after that. Also, instead of 3 cups of heavy cream, I used one cup of heavy cream and one cup of 2% milk.

text:
Love this recipe!
So easy and full of flavor. I got a lot of compliments on it..
Of course traditional butter chicken is made with boneless chicken breast but it tastes as good with whole chicken; especially for those who prefer thighs. Instead of baking the chicken, I cooked it in a sauce pan with the same amount of cooking oil because I don't like to wait for the oven to preheat :P. I replaced the 15 ounce tomato sauce with a 12 ounce tomato past, it has less water so the sauce takes less time to reach the thickness I want. 
It's great with rice, pita bread, or Naan bread
Defiantly a recipe to try!

Our family of 4 found this to be quite tasty and there were no leftovers! I followed the directions of another reviewer! To cut back on the amount of pans used, carmelize onions & garlic in butter, add sauces, and I found that I needed to let it simmer on a very low heat for approximately 30 minutes prior to adding chicken. Then simmered another 25-30 minutes to cook the chicken. One added note, I don't know about anyone else's grocery store, but I did not find garam marsala OR tandoori marsala in the ethnic OR the spice aisle of any grocery store in my general area. I found other spices that contained similar ingredients, and that is what I used in place of the garam marsala and the tandoori marsala. Still very good and we will definitely make this again.

I made this dish today and it was absolutely fantastic! It tasted exactly like the Butter Chicken that I order from my favorite Indian Restaurant, Bombay Cafe. I used the lower fat option the original writer of the recipe suggested with a few minor modifications. Since I had a 1/4 cup of heavy cream in the fridge, I added that along with the can of evap. I used only one stick of butter in the sauce (1/2 cup). The butter that I used was KerryGold Pure Irish Butter which has great flavor. I only used 1 and 1/2 tsp of salt instead of 2 as previous reviewers suggested. I used 2 pounds of boneless skinless chicken thighs cut up instead of chicken breasts because I prefer dark meat and I added 1 packet of Equal sweetner to the sauce which really brought out even more flavor. For those who had a hard time finding the different Masala seasonings, try going to an Indian grocery store. That is where I found them. I used the Garam Masala mix by Shan. It was $1.99 for a small box and I used the Tandoori barbeque Masala mix by MDH which was $1.59 for a box. Not that it should make a difference, but for those that might be interested, I used a Vidalia onion which is a little sweeter than a plain yellow onion, minced garlic in a jar by Spice World, the 15oz can of tomato sauce by Contadina and for the evaporated milk, I used the Carnation brand. Finally, I have a Nu-Wave oven so after seasoning the chicken chunks with the Tandoori Masala mixture, I put them in the Nu-wave and cooked them fo

text:
I made the lightened version of this dish with 2% evaporated milk and 1/4 cup butter.  I know this all seems like a lot of fat, but you need to have fat, properly emulsified, to get the right texture to the sauce.  Low fat = watery cream of tomato soup texture.   I felt that there was more than enough salt in the butter and tomato sauce, so I did not add any to the recipe.  You can always add it at the table, but you cant take it out! I like Indian foods and spices, so I upped the garam masala a tad and put a little freshly ground coriander in as well.  Marinating your chicken in spices and baking it separately is an important step in getting the flavour and texture just right.  Theres no point in wasting good ingredients by not following basic instructions.  This makes quite a lot of sauce, so I scoop out and freeze a small container of it to use on leftover chicken breast.

text:
Quite good, but a couple of suggestions.  First, follow the updated/experimental recipe suggested by the original submitter here in the comments to lower the amount of butter to 1/4 cup, and use a can of evaporated skim milk instead of the heavy cream.  Second, if you're fairly spice averse (like me), I'd recommend using little to no cayenne pepper.  The indian spice mixes already have some of this heat built in, and I find it a little more preferable to my (admittedly boring) Midwestern American palate.

text:
I made this in one skillet using mn's suggestions for change, which were using 4 Tablespoons of butter and evaporated skim milk. I browned the onions and garlic first, removed them from the skillet, browned the chicken pieces which I had sprinkled with a little garam masala (didn't have tandoori masala)and drizzled with oil, then added the butter and all the rest of the ingredients with the onion/garlic mixture and cooked it enough to blend the flavors. I added only one 12 oz. can of evaporated skim milk because I wanted the sauce thicker. I must say the next time I will add the evaporated skim milk last because even though I didn't boil it, it did start to curdle a little so I stopped the cooking right away. At first taste I thought it was too strong of a flavor but when I served it over rice it was incredible! I loved it. It would also be good with naan bread. The leftovers were fantastic the next day for lunch as well. This is a very flavorful dish that did not take very long to prepare. Easy and delicious.

text:
Great recipe! I used the "light" version (1/4 c. butter, 1 can evaporated milk, 1 can light coconut milk) and made minor alterations. Doubled the onion, added all spices to onion/garlic after 10 minutes and sauteed everything for 5 more. Then added all liquids and pureed everything together in a blender until smooth. Then put the sauce back on the stove to simmer. I started the chicken in another pan and when about half cooked, added it to the sauce to simmer on low until done. Served with Basmati rice. My family RAVED about dinner! Thanks so much!

text:
I've made butter chicken numerous times for my family in the past - we love the complexity of flavors that can be achieved even in a mild curry. Wanting a quicker version of the awesomely delicious restaurant style butter chicken I usually make, I decided to try this recipe out. Not a fan. This curry is bland, very heavy and is much too creamy, and is definitely lacking any depth of flavor. I doubled the amount of garam masala because all I could taste was butter and cream, and even then there's just so much missing from the curry. Sorry, I really wanted to love this, but I'm going to be sticking to my usual recipe that includes ginger paste, tomato paste/puree, and fenugreek leaves. All in all, this recipe is for someone who wants something easy, extremely mild and extremely (overly) creamy.

text:
The first time I made this recipe, I didn't have heavy cream, garam masala, or tandoori masala. As I usually do when I'm cooking, I substitute stuff and have fun with it. So instead of the gm and tm, I used ground cinnamon, black pepper, ground tumeric, and ground ginger. Before adding the onions and garlic to the butter, I put the spices in the butter until it got all brown and sizzly. Then I added the onions and garlic. When that got all caramelized and fragrant, I added a can of tomato sauce and salt to taste. Instead of heavy cream, I stirred in a couple of tablespoons of sour cream I had left in the fridge, and drizzled in milk while stirring until it looked like butter chicken sauce. For the chicken, I just baked it in the oven for 40 minutes at 375F, chopped it in cubes and threw it in the sauce. Simmered it while I cooked the basmati rice. It was AMAZING!!

Today I made the recipe closer to what this one calls for (though I only used 1 cup of table cream, and half a cup of butter). It's still delicious, but not as fragrant. I think the difference is I forgot to add the spices to the butter until it got all brown and sizzly!

I will definitely keep working to perfect this. So easy and fun to make. Yum!!

Loved it. Combination of original and other reviewers created a simple, low-fat, one-pot version: caramelized the onions with the garlic and some butter; added everything else except the chicken and simmered gently for 10 minutes; added the chicken, a green pepper, and a few carrots and simmered for 25 minutes. Swapped the tandoori masala for curry powder, and swapped the cream for a can of coconut milk and a can of evaporated milk. Cut the butter to 1/3 C total and reduced the salt to 1 t.

The easiest and tastiest butter chicken I've done! I just sauted garlic and onions together till light brown then added the spices, since I didn't have tandoori masala substituted it with meat masala and added 1 more teaspoon chilly powder ( we love spicy foods!), stir-fried for a minute then added the chicken pieces and cooked till brown, add tomato sauce, simmer till chicken is cooked then poured the cream and stirred until just bubbling!

text:
This is the best easy recipe we've found so far for butter chicken. A great starting point but could be improved with a few more spices. I plan on experimenting with what I have in my spice cabinet, such as coriander, ginger, cardamom, etc until I find the perfect combination.   We used about 1/2 of the butter and about one cup of light cream. We also added some Ginger to the sauce and I'd highly recommend skipping the added salt as it's unnecessary.   For the chicken, I coated mine in curry powder, paprika, and chili pepper before marinating in tandoori paste. I'd recommend marinating for a few hours to let the flavors sink in.   Be sure to serve over fragrant rice, like basmati.

text:
I never knew making butter chicken at home was so easy! I love making things a little more healthy (and using what I have on hand). Sauteed onion n garlic in 1/4 c butter, added 1tbsp garam masala and 1 tbsp curry powder, 2 shakes of cayenne, 1 small can tomato paste, and 1 cup warmed milk with 2 tbsp coffee mate mixed in. Warmed that mixture then added the raw bite size chicken breast pieces and simmered covered for 15 mins. Garnished with fresh cilantro and served with brown basmati rice. SO GOOD! Thanks so much!

My husband said it's the best thing he's ever eaten!  I did make a few changes.  I made it in a crock pot for four hours on high, so I didn't want to add the cream at the beginning and have it boil for that long.  I caramelized the onions and garlic  then added them to the pot with the chicken, spices (I had to use curry, paprika, and a dash of chili powder because of lack of masala), can of tomato paste and enough veggie broth and a splash of white wine to make a sauce. I just had to make a few alterations for the situation.

text:
Wonderful recipe! This is one of my favorite Indian dishes, and this is by far the easiest recipe I've seen, and it tastes just like I'd expect.
I followed a few of the suggestions from other reviewers to make a significantly healthier version. I cut down the butter to 1/4 cup as suggested by the author, omitted the oil and cream, and doubled the masala to 2 tsp. Probably not as rich tasting as the original, but we loved it.

I cooked the onions in a large stockpot, and then added the sauce ingredients to the same pan. I used some leftover cooked chicken and didn't have any tandori spices, so I just added the chicken to the sauce and let it simmer on low for awhile.

Pretty good butter chicken. I'm not sure this is as good as the "authentic" stuff at India House, but it's darn close (especially for making it at home). I really didn't want to consume 2 sticks of butter and 3 cups of heavy cream, but was afraid that a low-fat version just wouldn't taste the same (and I was  craving the REAL stuff). Next time, I'll try it with less butter and evaporated milk as submitter "mn" suggests. I found garam & tandoori masala at a local spice specialty store (I think using these spices makes all the difference - the $'s spent were so minimal, it was totally justified). I followed the recipe to a T except for adding a bit of cornstarch (mixed with water) and bringing to a boil during the final cooking step (I thought the sauce was too thin otherwise). Served over basmati rice with a sprinkling of fresh cilantro and a side of naan. Deeeelicious!!!! Thanks for sharing : )

Very nice recipe to build upon. The one I made used 10% cream and only 1/3 cup butter, but I made it simmer for 45 minutes. Also, since spices tend to lose some of their flavour after a long simmer, after stirring in the chicken, I added an additional 1/3 portion of all the spices mentionned, as well as 1/4 cup lemon juice and some tabasco.

I also did not have tandoori masala -- which is just a pre-made mixture -- so I just used the equivalent 2 tbs of garam masala, garlic, ginger, cumin, cayenne pepper and lemon juice.

Excellent! My husband is not normally fan of exotic spices but said this was really good! I served it over jasmine rice. I only used half of the cream and I cooked this in one large pot, so I didnt use the oil on the chicken. Glad we like it because now I have the spices!

text:
Worked out well making this casein-free with dairy-free Greek yogurt alternate and ghee.  After browning, I bloomed the spices then added the rest of the sauce ingredients. I used skin-on bone-in chicken quarters (leg with thigh attached) and dry rubbed the tandoori then set it sit for 30 mins, then added more tandoori rub and then baked at 425 for 20 mins skin-side down.  Turned chicken over and turned oven down to 375 and baked for another 20 mins. Removed from oven and added to the sauce (along with any crispy pan bits) then followed the recipe from that point forward.  Served with rice cooker saffron rice and mustard seed roasted green beans (using some of the rendered chicken fat from the roasting pan).

Sauteed the onion, 2 garlic cloves, some minced ginger in a couple of tablespoons of butter.  Once caramelized, I added the cayenne and garam masala and let the spices toast until fragrant.  Added the tomato sauce and a little over a cup of cream.  Then I added in the chicken and simmered until cooked.  I added fresh chopped spinach and chopped cilantro right before serving with some spiced basmati rice.  It was the best home cooked Indian dish I've made, thanks for the delicious recipe, and excellent advice from the author and  those of you who cooked this previously.  I will be making this again and try with the evaporated milk.  Oh and I added a couple of teaspoons of sugar as someone else recommended.

text:
Soooo good, it tastes as good as an Indian Restaurant, perfect amount of spiciness for me (I dont like too much heat), but easily adjustable if you prefer more of a kick!

The only adjustments I made were to replace half the heavy cream with condensed milk, and I added yellow tumeric and yellow squash lightly sauteed. 

I did have an issue with the thickness of the sauce, it seemed a bit runny to me even after simmering 40 minutes. I just put like 2 Tablespoons of flour in it. It thickened right up and I couldn't taste the flour at all!

I was new to cooking Indian and this was not intimidating like most recipes are with the ingredient list, but the pay off was amazing! My wife and I will be raving about this for weeks!

I had much higher expectation based on other reviews.  I used the heavy cream and butter despite lower calorie options.  This dish is perfectly find for a normal weekday dinner.  But this in no way resembles real Indian food.  The dish is bland.  It should be dramatically more spicy.  This seems like one of those dishes people who never travel make and think it's authentic.  It's nothing like the Butter Chicken you will find at an authentic Indian restaurant in your area.  It's edible.  I guess it's good if you have kids or fear of the heat used in Asia by half of the world's population.

But I won't make this again.  It doesn't even closely resemble true authentic Indian Butter Chicken.  It's the super watered down American version.

I've made this both with both the original recipe and the lower fat version with 1/4 butter (instead of 1 cup) and 1 can of evaporated skim milk, and I liked the lower fat version better. This is by far the best butter chicken recipe I've tried.  I used the low fat version - 1/4 C butter and 1 can no-fat carnation milk.  I didn't put any cayenne pepper in it because I don't like heat.  Next time I'll cut the butter to 1/8 C to see how that works.    We are vegetarian so instead of chicken, I put the tandoori masala  in with some bread crumbs, diped cauliflower in a mixture of egg white, water and oil, and shook in the bread crumb mixture, then deep fried for about 5 minutes.  Delicious.

text:
I searched for hours looking for a recipe for Butter Chicken that was just like my favorite Indian restaurant. Then I reviewed many of the reviews for this recipe, noting the modifications and suggestions therein.  I made it very, very close to as written in the original. The only changes:  I added 2 Tsp of brown sugar (I always add sugar, when using tomato sauces, to cut the acidic effect). I also used rounded teaspoons on the garam masala.  Also, I made sure to cut the chicken into small pieces, which helped them bake faster in the oven (I baked it for 20 minutes).  
I must say, it came out PERFECT, and I couldn't be happier. I would not change a thing, except inasmuch as I am a chili-head, if I made this JUST for me (and not my finicky kids and wife) I MIGHT (probably not) double the garam masala and the red pepper...or add some ghost pepper flakes.  That's just me though. Honestly, Butter Chicken is SUPPOSED to be mild, and in truth I have never encountered it spicy-hot.

text:
I made this tonight and it was wonderful!! I did make a few changes, I used 1/2 cup of butter instead of 1, and also used 2 cups of cream and 1 cup of milk instead of 3 cups of cream. For the chicken, I took the advice of one of the reviewers and made a mixture of 1/3 cup of honey yogurt, half a lemon juice,  a dash of cayenne pepper, 1 tbsp of garam masala, 1 tbsp curry powder, a light sprinkle of chili powder, mixed it all together with the cut up chicken pieces and grilled it outside in a grill pan until fully cooked. This added a depth of flavor and smokiness to the butter sauce that was absolutely DIVINE!!! There were compliments all through dinner, I served with grilled garlic naan bread, coconut rice and sauteed asparagus. Try it this way, you will not regret it!

AMAZING recipe! I adjusted the amounts of some of the spices according to taste, but overall, this recipe is perfect.

I'm not a good cook by any means, but this recipe was super easy for even a novice like me. I can't get enough of the sauce. I added chipotle peppers (on hand), and it complimented the other spices.

text:
LOVE IT! I did however make some changes to this recipe to make it healthier and milk free.

First for a milk free recipe, I substituted canned coconut milk for the heavy cream. Make sure it is the good stuff that is super thick when it comes out of the can. You can also mix it up with more liquid coconut milks if you think it is too thick. (I prefer a thicker sauce, but some people don't) also... (BE SURE IT IS UNSWEETENED!) Sometimes I get the kind in the carton at the store (unsweetened of course!) and mix half of that with half canned. It depends on the consistency you want.  The butter can be substituted with coconut oil and I found that I didn't need as much butter (or oil) as the recipe called for. So use less! (You can use up to 1/4 of the amount stated in the recipe and it will be fine.)

Another way I have made this is by substituting the heavy cream with the following ingredients:
Yogurt, greek yogurt, sour cream, milk, kefir  (all unflavored and unsweetened)

Usually I just mix these together until I have the right consistency and amount needed for the recipe. Every time it has come out good! 

Note:  Some yogurts, Kefir and especially sour cream give it a stronger taste. Some people do not like this, so please, taste your milk based mix before adding to be sure you don't mess with the flavor. 

Also I have made this recipe in which I did half coconut and half dairy and it came out great. Its a pretty flexible recipe and comes out great every time!

Hope I was hel

text:
I made a few changes to this recipe. I used half and half butter and canola oil and cut it back to about 1/2 a cup. Instead of cream I use 0% Greek Yogurt but I add it at THE END. Before I do this I strain off any surface oil. By adding the yogurt at the end there is less risk of it it curdling with the tomatoes. However if  it does curdle a good tip to know is simply blend it in a blender until it's smooth. It works perfectly every time. I also 'play' with the spices I just made it with Sharwood's hot madras curry,  a generic Garam Marsala, some cumin, cayenne and a bit of Anjo Chili powder. I do cook the onions and garlic separately  and add them later. I think it tastes better this way. Instead of cutting the chicken breasts into chunks I coat them (whole)  with Garam Marsala and Anjo Chili powder, and put them in a 425  degree hot oven for 30 minutes (for 4 boneless breasts). This way they are really juicy when you cut them up into chunks and fold them into the sauce with the caramelized onions. All in all this is a solid basic recipe with authentic and delicious flavour. Thank you for posting it. It is my family's easy 'go to' butter chicken recipe, and we make it at least once a month.

text:
Absolutely delicious. This is an excellent recipe which goes to the head of my East Indian recipe list.
Changed up the recipe a bit. To adjust ease of preparation, I browned the chicken until just slightly underdone in the same pan used for the onion. When I returned the chicken to the mixture and simmered for 5 or 6 minutes, it was perfectly done. To adjust taste to my craving at the time, I used 3 teaspoons of curry powder instead of Garam Masala and Garam Masala to replace the tandoori masala.

Will try the low fat version next time. Not that I would miss doing the original version when I wanted to wow my company.

text:
This recipe is amazing.  Key is to caramelize the onions properly to give the sauce all that flavour.  I did make quite a few changes to take the fat content down.

I used half the butter
I used twice the chicken
1 substituted 3 cups of heavy cream for 1 cup of 18% cream and 1 cup 5% cream.  I also used my own frozen tomatos.   Added the sauce to the caramelized onions rather than the other way.  
Blended the sauce to avoid the lumpy onions to make smooth.

Served with Brown Basamati

I loved this recipe, best butter chicken I have ever had, however I did modify it a bit due to missing some ingredients and to lower the calories. Instead of the 3 cups of heavy cream I added 1 cup heavy cream and 2 cups of thick yogurt. Instead of the tomato sauce I used tomato paste and 1 cup of water.  Also I used 1/4 cup of butter and 2 teaspoons of garam masala.  If you want this to be a bit hotter up the cayenne but do so slowly as when this spice simmers it gets hotter, for those of you that don't know.

text:
I'm not a super experienced cook and this was pretty easy for me. The biggest pain I encountered was making the tandoori masala and garam masala spice mixes because my local store didn't have them (just google what spices go in and get those!). I also used cauliflower instead of chicken. Put it on a  cookie sheet and tossed in olive oil and tandoori masala and oven roasted them. This sauce recipe is to die for, my husband says it's one of the most delicious things I've ever cooked! I've already recommended it to a few friends and highly recommend to anyone considering making it! I used 1/4 butter but still used the heavy cream. Served the cauliflower over rice with the sauce and some naan bread.

text:
This was delicious!  Had my whole house smelling like an Indian restaurant :)  I did make a few modifications in the interest of trimming some of the fat/calories.  Instead of 3 cups heavy cream, I used 1 cup heavy cream and 2 cups fat free half & half.  Also, I only used 1/2 cup butter for the entire recipe instead of 1 cup.  The sauce may have been a bit thinner because of these changes, but the rice seemed to absorb it during the eating.  Also, it had a creamy texture and taste, but wasn't too heavy.  I couldn't find tandoori masala like everyone else, so I found a recipe for the spice mix on Food.com - my cupboard had all of the spices except mace, fenugreek, and cardamom (and I left out the red food coloring).  The spice mix was still delicious on the chicken!

text:
I made this last night and found it very, as it says in the title, EASY! I made a few changes, as I see a lot of people have. I made the sauce all in one pan - First caramelizing the onions and garlic in butter. I then made a sauce out of tomato paste (half a can), heavy cream, coconut milk I had left over from making coconut rice to go with this dish, water and some whole milk, all the seasoning listed above -- Then I added more butter to the pan with the onions and garlic but not as much as this recipe requires - In total I used 1/2 cup of butter. Then I added my sauce mixture to the pan and let simmer as instructed above. While that was simmering - I took out my chicken which I had previously already cleaned and seasoned with lime, garlic powder, pinch of salt and the tandoori masala which was marinating all day. I then pan fried that until golden brown on each side of the cubes --- Then added some SPINACH to the sauce that was simmering. I took a baking dish out and put the chicken on the bottom of it - And then poured the sauce all over and baked at 375 for half an hour. With the coconut brown rice, it was really really good. I have eaten my fair share of butter chicken, some of the best in Vancouver, B.C. and this came out pretty similar BUT I found it wasn't as sweet as other butter chicken I have had.. I think next time, to experiment, I may add a teaspoon of sugar.. sweetness and the spicy works well and again I notice all butter chicken I have had was sweeter.

This was good spice wise, but I did a few things differently to reduce cals and save time. I didn't use any butter, but rather sauteed the onions, garlic garam marsala and tandoori masala together to obtain more flavor. I used 1 can of lite coconut milk and 1 cup of cream to reduce fat. I didn't have any tomato sauce, so I used about 1.5 cans of tomato paste. I also added 3 potatoes chopped up. I removed the baking step and added the chicken to the coconut milk, cream and spices once they had started to simmer. I let it simmer for about 30 minutes before enjoying with rice. It was really good.

text:
I've been cooking this recipe for a while now, normally just for myself. I found a shortcut in cooking the chicken, so instead of baking it in the oven, grill the tandoori chicken and onion in a sauce pan (it's coated in oil anyway) until the pieces look almost done, then add the tomato sauce, heavy cream, and spices. Let simmer for about 5 mins, then add the butter. To get an idea of how much sauce I'm producing jus for myself, I usually just add 2 large spoonful of tomato sauce and about 1/4 cup of heavy cream. That should be enough for the chicken and whatever side you use (either rice or naan). It's quick and easy and done within 30 mins. Love it!

It definitely isn't perfect butter chicken but it's probably the best I'll ever make. Good Indian food recipes are so hard to get your hands on. I am Indian so this rating includes an authenticity factor. It's very rich and the chicken came out delicious. The other popular butter chicken recipe on the site came out horrible when I made it and I think it was the difference between using heavy cream and sour cream. Overall an excellent recipe! I substituted with 1/2 cup butter and 1 can evap milk for the heavy cream, and it worked fine. I added 2x garam masala (before simmering for 30 mins) because I did a taste test and thought it needed more flavour...however I don't know if it was necessary since the flavours could've been stronger after simmering. I also marinated the chicken with tandoori masala, salt and pepper for a couple hrs prior to baking. Finally, I took a star off because although it's a good recipe, it's still not as great as some of the butter chicken I've had at restaurants. In general, it's a solid recipe!

text:
I just made this last night and it was tasty! I tried to improvise since I didn't have any heavy cream, so I tried to make heavy cream my self: big mistake. The sauce didn't thicken as expected, but I added some corn starch, which solved the problem. I also didn't have any tandori masala, so I seasoned the chicken with garam masala, which tasted excellent. It was a bit too buttery for me, but that could be because I decided to make my own cream. Next time, I will definitely buy the cream.
The chicken took a lot longer to cook than 12 minutes: I put it on broil for 5 minutes after 15 minutes of baking, which made it a bit drier, but the chicken has a lot of juices on the pan and in the meat. 
I will definitely be making this again: pretty easy to make and delicious.

text:
FANTASTIC recipe!! I'm fussy with my indian food, but this was incredible and a breeze to make. I made a couple of changes. I mixed the chicken with the oil and masala then fried it in the pan that had previously sauteed the onion and garlic for about 5 mins then added the sauce to it. I left it to cook for over an hour then added the cream before serving. I also added a tsp of curry powder and increased the garam masala to 1 tbsp. It was amazing!! I will cut back on the amount of butter next time as it was too much, and the salt wasn't needed. But a very authentic tasting recipe
Edit: When making the sauce do not mince the garlic and onion, rather finely chop and fry. Cook with the tomato and spices on low for as many hours as you can (the flavour really comes out) then puree with a wand blender. I manage to use only 2 pans when making this. I am now CONSTANTLY asked to make this and is several of my friends favourite dish that I cook. Thanks so much for this recipe.

text:
I too tried this recipe because of the short ingredient list, and it's great!  I did buy the called for indian spices and recommend doing so if you are going to make this, as tandoori masala is a different taste than straight curry powder.  I cut back the butter to 1/4 C and one can of evap skim milk, per the author's suggestion and it was still incredibly tasty.  I also think the suggestion of 1-2 t sugar is a good one, I didn't do that but will next time.  1/2 t red pepper is enough if you don't like spicy butter chicken.   Try it out, it's very authentic!

text:
Wow, this was so good! The short ingredient list drew me in but also made me a little hesitant. Boy was I ever wrong! This was our first attempt at an Indian dish and we couldn't get enough! This makes 4 very large portions, and we are looking forward to the leftovers tonight!   I know it's butter chicken, but small changes make a world of difference in cutting back fat. We used 1/2 cup butter, 2 tbsp garlic, 2 cups heavy cream, 1 small can of evaporated milk and the rest milk. Some store-bought naan and a pot of basmati rice rounded out our meal. There many steps and quite a few dishes to wash, but the end result is worth it!    Next time we might add some tomato paste to thicken the sauce. But otherwise the recipe is perfect, as is! Thank you!

Excellent. Super easy and very tasty. Mine was similar to the suggested low-fat version - I used a can of coconut milk instead of cream, and only about 1/3 cup margarine in total. Hate making extra dishes so I did it all in one pan: browned the chicken with the onions, then added all the rest till it was cooked through. I did simmer till it had boiled down quite a bit (even using a smaller volume of liquid than suggested I found it a bit runny). If the contributor hadn't added a low-fat option I would only have given this four stars, since even with only 1/3 cup marg it was rather greasy and I can't IMAGINE what it would have been like with all that cream and butter.

text:
We really enjoyed this.  Even my 2- and 4-year old picky eaters ate all their chicken!  I substituted 1 can evap. milk as the author suggested in a review, along with 1/2 can coconut milk and ony 1 cup cream. I only used 2/3 cup butter (might cut that to 1/2 cup next time) and 1/2 tsp cayenne (DH and I can add sriracha at the table but my children won't eat it if it is too spicy).  I also added a small pinch brown sugar to temper the acidic salty tomato taste (not enough to make the sauce sweet though).  I couldn't find tandoori masala, so I subsititued a mix of curry powder, garam masala, and corander.  I browned the chicken in the pan I used for the onons and then poured the sauce over and let it simmer on low and it turned out perfectly tender and flavorful.  We had a TON of extra sauce so we will have this dish again soon!  DH is looking forward to dipping some naan in the sauce for a snack as well.  I was worried this wouldn't be too authentic, but it tasted just like that at our local Indian restaurant and we loved it.  Thanks!
